</p><p>The Somewhere Back in Time World Tour continued with two further legs in the US and Europe in the summer of 2008, during which the band used a more expansive stage-set, including further elements of the original <i>Live After Death</i> show.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESputnikmusic2008_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESputnikmusic2008-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> With the sole UK concert taking place at <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham Stadium</a>, this would be the first time the band would headline a stadium in their own country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThrash_Hits2007_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThrash_Hits2007-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The three 2008 legs of the tour were remarkably successful; it was the second highest-grossing tour of the year for a British artist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKhan2009_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKhan2009-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The last part of the tour took place in February and March 2009, with the band, once again, using "Ed Force One".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2008_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2008-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The final leg included the band's first ever appearances in Peru and Ecuador, as well as their return to Venezuela and New Zealand after 17 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESoto2008_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESoto2008-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The band also played another show in India (their third in the country within a span of 2 years) at the <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock in India">Rock in India</a> festival to a crowd of 20,000. At their concert in São Paulo on 15 March, Dickinson announced on stage that it was the largest non-festival show of their career, with an overall attendance of 63,000&#160;people.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKaczuroski2009_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaczuroski2009-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> The final leg ended in Florida on 2 April after which the band took a break. Overall, the tour reportedly had an attendance of over two million people worldwide over both years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2009d_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2009d-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/2009_BRIT_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 BRIT Awards">2009 BRIT Awards</a>, Iron Maiden won the award for best British live act.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2009b_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2009b-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Voted for by the public, the band reportedly won by a landslide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2009c_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2009c-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 January 2009, the band announced that they were to release a full-length documentary film in select cinemas on 21 April 2009. Entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden:_Flight_666" title="Iron Maiden: Flight 666">Iron Maiden: Flight 666</a></i>, it was filmed during the first part of the Somewhere Back in Time World Tour between February and March 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2009a_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2009a-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> <i>Flight 666</i> was co-produced by Banger Productions and was distributed in cinemas by Arts Alliance Media and <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>, with <a href="/wiki/D%26E_Entertainment" title="D&amp;E Entertainment">D&amp;E Entertainment</a> sub-distributing in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2009d_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2009d-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The film went on to have a Blu-ray, DVD, and CD release in May and June,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2009d_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2009d-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> topping the music DVD charts in 22 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2009f_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2009f-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="The_Final_Frontier_and_Maiden_England_World_Tour_.282010.E2.80.932014.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Final_Frontier_and_Maiden_England_World_Tour_(2010–2014)"><i>The Final Frontier</i> and Maiden England World Tour (2010–2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Final Frontier and Maiden England World Tour (2010–2014)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/The_Final_Frontier" title="The Final Frontier">The Final Frontier</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Final_Frontier_World_Tour" title="The Final Frontier World Tour">The Final Frontier World Tour</a>, <a href="/wiki/En_Vivo!_(Iron_Maiden_album)" title="En Vivo! (Iron Maiden album)">En Vivo! (Iron Maiden album)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maiden_England_World_Tour" title="Maiden England World Tour">Maiden England World Tour</a></div>
<p>Following announcements that the band had begun composition of new material and booked studio time in early 2010 with <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Shirley" title="Kevin Shirley">Kevin Shirley</a> producing,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMasters2009_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMasters2009-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Final_Frontier" title="The Final Frontier">The Final Frontier</a></i> was announced on 4 March.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2010a_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2010a-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The album, the band's fifteenth, was released on 16 August,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010c_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010c-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> garnering critical acclaim<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetaCritic1_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetaCritic1-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> and the band's greatest commercial success in their history, reaching No.&#160;1 in twenty-eight countries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman2011_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman2011-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Although Steve Harris had been quoted in the past as claiming that the band would only produce fifteen studio releases,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDaily_Star2009_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaily_Star2009-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> band members have since confirmed that there will be at least one further record.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2010bDawson2011_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2010bDawson2011-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album's <a href="/wiki/The_Final_Frontier_World_Tour" title="The Final Frontier World Tour">supporting tour</a> saw the band perform 98 shows across the globe to an estimated audience of over 2 million,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2011a_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2011a-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> including their first visits to Singapore, Indonesia, and South Korea,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman2011_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman2011-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> before concluding in London on 6 August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010f_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010f-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> As the tour's 2010 leg preceded <i>The Final Frontier</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s release, the band made "<a href="/wiki/El_Dorado_(Iron_Maiden_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="El Dorado (Iron Maiden song)">El Dorado</a>" available as a free download on 8 June,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010c_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010c-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> which would go on to win the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Metal Performance">Best Metal Performance</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Grammy Awards">2011 Grammy Awards</a> on 13 February 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010g_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010g-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> It was the band's first win following two previous Grammy nominations ("<a href="/wiki/Fear_of_the_Dark_(song)" title="Fear of the Dark (song)">Fear of the Dark</a>" in 1994 and "<a href="/wiki/The_Wicker_Man_(song)" title="The Wicker Man (song)">The Wicker Man</a>" in 2001).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERock_on_the_Net_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERock_on_the_Net-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 March, a new compilation to accompany 2009's <i><a href="/wiki/Somewhere_Back_in_Time" title="Somewhere Back in Time">Somewhere Back in Time</a></i> was announced. Entitled <i><a href="/wiki/From_Fear_to_Eternity_(album)" title="From Fear to Eternity (album)">From Fear to Eternity</a></i>, the original release date was set at 23 May, but was later delayed to 6 June.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2011c_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2011c-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The double disc set covers the period 1990–2010 (the band's most recent eight studio albums),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2011c_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2011c-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> and, as on <i>Somewhere Back in Time</i>, live versions with <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Dickinson" title="Bruce Dickinson">Bruce Dickinson</a> were included in place of original recordings which featured other vocalists, in this case <a href="/wiki/Blaze_Bayley" title="Blaze Bayley">Blaze Bayley</a>.
</p><p>In a press release regarding <i>From Fear to Eternity</i>, band manager <a href="/wiki/Rod_Smallwood" title="Rod Smallwood">Rod Smallwood</a> revealed that Iron Maiden would release a new concert video to DVD in 2011, filmed in Santiago, Chile and Buenos Aires, Argentina during The Final Frontier World Tour.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrave_Words_&amp;_Bloody_Knuckles2011_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrave_Words_&amp;_Bloody_Knuckles2011-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> On 17 January 2012, the band announced that the new release, entitled <i><a href="/wiki/En_Vivo!_(Iron_Maiden_album)" title="En Vivo! (Iron Maiden album)">En Vivo!</a></i>, based on footage from the Chile concert, would be made available worldwide on CD, LP, DVD, and Blu-ray on 26 March, except for the United States and Canada (where it was released on 27 March).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2012_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2012-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the concert footage, the video release includes an 88-minute tour documentary, entitled Behind The Beast, containing interviews with the band and their crew.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUpVenue_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUpVenue-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, one song from the release ("Blood Brothers") was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Hard_Rock/Metal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Hard Rock/Metal Performance">Grammy Award for Best Hard Rock/Metal Performance</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2013_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 Grammy Awards">2013 Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlderslade2012b_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlderslade2012b-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 February 2012, the band announced the <a href="/wiki/Maiden_England_World_Tour" title="Maiden England World Tour">Maiden England World Tour</a> 2012–14, which was based around the <a href="/wiki/Maiden_England" title="Maiden England">video of the same name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlderslade2012a_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlderslade2012a-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The tour commenced in North America in the summer of 2012 and was followed by further dates in 2013 and 2014, which included the band's record-breaking fifth headline performance at <a href="/wiki/Donington_Park" title="Donington Park">Donington Park</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKielty2012_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKielty2012-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> their first show at the newly built <a href="/wiki/Friends_Arena" title="Friends Arena">national stadium</a> in Stockholm,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENilsson2012_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENilsson2012-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> a return to the <a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio</a> festival in Brazil,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChilders2012Rocha2012_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChilders2012Rocha2012-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> and their debut appearance in Paraguay.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrónica2013_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrónica2013-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> In August 2012, Steve Harris stated that the <i>Maiden England</i> video would be re-issued in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJaedike2012_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJaedike2012-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> with a release date later set for 25 March 2013 in DVD, CD, and LP formats under the title <i>Maiden England '88</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHartmann2013_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHartmann2013-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="The_Book_of_Souls_and_Legacy_of_the_Beast_.282015.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Book_of_Souls_and_Legacy_of_the_Beast_(2015–present)"><i>The Book of Souls</i> and <i>Legacy of the Beast</i> (2015–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The Book of Souls and Legacy of the Beast (2015–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Souls" title="The Book of Souls">The Book of Souls</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Souls_World_Tour" title="The Book of Souls World Tour">The Book of Souls World Tour</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Legacy_of_the_Beast_World_Tour" title="Legacy of the Beast World Tour">Legacy of the Beast World Tour</a></div>
<p>Following confirmation from the group that 2010's <i>The Final Frontier</i> would not be their last album,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2010bDawson2011_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2010bDawson2011-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Bruce Dickinson revealed plans for a sixteenth studio record in July 2013, with a potential release date in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETez2013_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETez2013-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In February 2015, drummer Nicko McBrain revealed that a new album had been completed, although the release was put on hold as Dickinson was recovering from treatment for a cancerous tumour found on his tongue.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKielty2015aKaufman2015_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKielty2015aKaufman2015-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> On 15 May, after Dickinson was cleared for activities, manager Rod Smallwood confirmed that the album would be released in 2015, although the band would not tour until 2016 to allow Dickinson to continue recuperating.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMunro2015_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMunro2015-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>  On 18 June 2015, the band's website announced its title, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Souls" title="The Book of Souls">The Book of Souls</a></i>, and confirmed a release date of 4 September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrow2015_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrow2015-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> It is the band's first original studio album not to be issued by EMI outside North America, following <a href="/wiki/Parlophone" title="Parlophone">Parlophone</a>'s acquisition by <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Group</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris2013_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris2013-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> A critical and commercial success, it received positive reviews and became the band's fifth UK No. 1 album.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetaCritic2Sexton2015_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetaCritic2Sexton2015-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:IronMaidenO2_270517-24_(34145654484).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/IronMaidenO2_270517-24_%2834145654484%29.jpg/220px-IronMaidenO2_270517-24_%2834145654484%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/IronMaidenO2_270517-24_%2834145654484%29.jpg/330px-IronMaidenO2_270517-24_%2834145654484%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/IronMaidenO2_270517-24_%2834145654484%29.jpg/440px-IronMaidenO2_270517-24_%2834145654484%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5864" data-file-height="3308" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:IronMaidenO2_270517-24_(34145654484).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Smith, Harris, Murray and Gers performing in 2017.</div></div></div>
<p>The new record was recorded at Guillaume Tell Studios, Paris, which they had previously used for 2000's <i>Brave New World</i>, with regular producer Kevin Shirley in late summer 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKielty2015b_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKielty2015b-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> With a total run time of 92 minutes, it is the group's first double studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKielty2015b_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKielty2015b-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the release's closing song, "<a href="/wiki/Empire_of_the_Clouds" title="Empire of the Clouds">Empire of the Clouds</a>", penned by Dickinson, surpassed "Rime of the Ancient Mariner" (from 1984's <i>Powerslave</i>) as Iron Maiden's longest song, at 18 minutes in length.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrow2015_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrow2015-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> A music video for the song "<a href="/wiki/Speed_of_Light_(Iron_Maiden_song)" title="Speed of Light (Iron Maiden song)">Speed of Light</a>" was issued on 14 August.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELach2015a_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELach2015a-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2016, the band embarked on <a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Souls_World_Tour" title="The Book of Souls World Tour">The Book of Souls World Tour</a>, which saw them play concerts in 35 countries in North and South America, Asia, Australasia, Africa, and Europe, including their first ever performances in China, El Salvador, and Lithuania.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELach2015bAlfa.lt2015_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELach2015bAlfa.lt2015-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> As with 2008–09's Somewhere Back in Time World Tour and 2010–11's The Final Frontier World Tour, the group travelled in a customised aeroplane, flown by Dickinson and nicknamed "Ed Force One", although they used a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> jumbo jet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELach2015b_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELach2015b-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The band completed the tour in 2017 with further European and North American shows.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELach2016bChilders2017_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELach2016bChilders2017-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> On 20 September 2017, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Souls:_Live_Chapter" title="The Book of Souls: Live Chapter">The Book of Souls: Live Chapter</a></i> was announced. Recorded throughout The Book of Souls World Tour, it was released on 17 November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBritton2017_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBritton2017-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the summer of 2016, the group launched a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_game" title="Mobile game">mobile game</a>, <i>Iron Maiden: Legacy of the Beast</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELach2016a_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELach2016a-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Inspired by the game's title, the band would undertake the <a href="/wiki/Legacy_of_the_Beast_World_Tour" title="Legacy of the Beast World Tour">Legacy of the Beast World Tour</a>, commencing in Europe in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMunro2017b_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMunro2017b-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> with North and South American shows following in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKreps2018_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKreps2018-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> On September 23rd, the band confirmed that the tour would extend into 2020, with two UK shows confirmed for Belsonic Festival in Belfast and a record seventh headline show at Donington Park, England, as part of Download Festival<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Image_and_legacy">Image and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Image and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Iron Maiden were ranked No.&#160;24 in <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s "100 Greatest Artists of Hard Rock",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVH12005_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVH12005-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> No.&#160;4 in <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s "Top 10 Greatest Heavy Metal Bands of All Time"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMTV2006(a)_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMTV2006(a)-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> and No.&#160;3 in <a href="/wiki/VH1_Classic" class="mw-redirect" title="VH1 Classic">VH1 Classic</a>'s "Top 20 Metal Bands".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVH12006_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVH12006-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>  The band also won the <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivor Novello Award">Ivor Novello Award</a> for international achievement in 2002<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESanctuary_Group2002_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESanctuary_Group2002-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> and were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Guitar_Center#Hollywood&#39;s_RockWalk" title="Guitar Center">Hollywood RockWalk</a> whilst touring in the US in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuitar_Center_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuitar_Center-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Iron Maiden frequently use the slogan "Up the Irons" in their disc liner notes, and the phrase can also be seen on several T-shirts officially licensed by the band. It is a paraphrase of "Up the Hammers", the phrase which refers to the London <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club, <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United" class="mw-redirect" title="West Ham United">West Ham United</a>, of which founder Steve Harris is a fan.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFootball_Fancast_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFootball_Fancast-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Iron Maiden's <a href="/wiki/Mascot" title="Mascot">mascot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eddie_(mascot)" title="Eddie (mascot)">Eddie</a>, is a perennial fixture in the band's science fiction and horror-influenced album cover art, as well as in <a href="/wiki/Concert" title="Concert">live</a> shows.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004133_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004133-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Originally a papier-mâché mask incorporated in their backdrop which would squirt fake blood during their live shows,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall200462_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall200462-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> the name would be transferred to the character featured in the band's debut album cover, created by <a href="/wiki/Derek_Riggs" title="Derek Riggs">Derek Riggs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004136_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004136-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Eddie was painted exclusively by Riggs until 1992, at which point the band began using artwork from numerous other artists as well, including <a href="/wiki/Melvyn_Grant" title="Melvyn Grant">Melvyn Grant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004289_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004289-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Eddie is also featured in the band's <a href="/wiki/First-person_shooter" title="First-person shooter">first-person shooter</a> video game, <i><a href="/wiki/Ed_Hunter" title="Ed Hunter">Ed Hunter</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPopoff2005(a)_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPopoff2005(a)-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> as well as their <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">mobile</a> <a href="/wiki/Role-playing_game" title="Role-playing game">role-playing game</a>, <i>Iron Maiden: Legacy of the Beast</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELach2016a_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELach2016a-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> in addition to numerous T-shirts, posters and other band-related merchandise.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004133_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004133-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, he was awarded the "Icon Award" at the <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Hammer" title="Metal Hammer">Metal Hammer</a></i> Golden Gods,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThrash_Hits2008_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThrash_Hits2008-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Guitar_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibson Guitar Corporation">Gibson.com</a> describes him as "the most recognisable metal icon in the world and one of the most versatile too".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELefkove2008_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELefkove2008-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Iron Maiden's distinct logo has adorned all of the band's releases since their debut, 1979's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Soundhouse_Tapes" title="The Soundhouse Tapes">The Soundhouse Tapes</a></i> EP. The typeface originates with <a href="/wiki/Vic_Fair" title="Vic Fair">Vic Fair</a>'s poster design for the 1976 science fiction film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Fell_to_Earth_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Man Who Fell to Earth (film)">The Man Who Fell to Earth</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMeansheets2010_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMeansheets2010-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> also used by <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Giltrap" title="Gordon Giltrap">Gordon Giltrap</a>, although Steve Harris claims that he designed it himself, using his abilities as an architectural draughtsman.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEMI1998_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEMI1998-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The song "<a href="/wiki/Always_Look_on_the_Bright_Side_of_Life" title="Always Look on the Bright Side of Life">Always Look on the Bright Side of Life</a>" (from <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python" title="Monty Python">Monty Python</a>’s <i><a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Life_of_Brian" title="Monty Python&#39;s Life of Brian">Life of Brian</a></i>) is a staple at their concerts, where the recording is played after the final encore.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2019, the band filed a $2 million lawsuit against video game company <a href="/wiki/3D_Realms" title="3D Realms">3D Realms</a> for infringing on their trademark via the planned release of a game called <a href="/wiki/Ion_Maiden" class="mw-redirect" title="Ion Maiden">Ion Maiden</a>, which the band claims “is nearly identical to the Iron Maiden trademark in appearance, sound and overall commercial impression.” The suit further accuses 3D Realms of causing “confusion among consumers” by depicting a skull icon similar to the band's Eddie mascot and that <i>Ion Maiden</i> is similar to the band's own <i>Legacy of the Beast</i> video game.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_on_other_artists">Influence on other artists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Influence on other artists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_World" title="Guitar World">Guitar World</a></i>, Iron Maiden's music has "influenced generations of newer metal acts, from legends like <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a> to current stars like <a href="/wiki/Avenged_Sevenfold" title="Avenged Sevenfold">Avenged Sevenfold</a>,"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBienstock2011_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBienstock2011-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> with Metallica drummer <a href="/wiki/Lars_Ulrich" title="Lars Ulrich">Lars Ulrich</a> commenting that he has "always had an incredible amount of respect and admiration for them."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerrang!2008_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerrang!2008-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kerry_King" title="Kerry King">Kerry King</a> of <a href="/wiki/Slayer" title="Slayer">Slayer</a> stated that "they meant so much to [him] in their early days" and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Ian" title="Scott Ian">Scott Ian</a> of <a href="/wiki/Anthrax_(American_band)" title="Anthrax (American band)">Anthrax</a> said that "they had a major impact on [his] life."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoung(2)_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoung(2)-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/M._Shadows" title="M. Shadows">M. Shadows</a> of Avenged Sevenfold stated that Iron Maiden "are by far the best live band in the world and their music is timeless", while <a href="/wiki/Trivium_(band)" title="Trivium (band)">Trivium</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Matt_Heafy" title="Matt Heafy">Matt Heafy</a> comments that "without Iron Maiden, Trivium surely wouldn't exist".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerrang!2008_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerrang!2008-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slipknot_(band)" title="Slipknot (band)">Slipknot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stone_Sour" title="Stone Sour">Stone Sour</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Corey_Taylor" title="Corey Taylor">Corey Taylor</a> said that "Steve Harris does more with four fingers than I've ever seen anybody do. And Bruce Dickinson? Dude! To me, he was the quintessential old-school heavy metal singer. He could hit notes that were just sick, and he was a great showman. Everything made me a fan. And there wasn't a dude that I hung out with that wasn't trying to draw Eddie on their schoolbooks",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMTV2006(a)_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMTV2006(a)-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> while their music also helped <a href="/wiki/Jesper_Str%C3%B6mblad" title="Jesper Strömblad">Jesper Strömblad</a> of <a href="/wiki/In_Flames" title="In Flames">In Flames</a> to pioneer the <a href="/wiki/Melodic_death_metal" title="Melodic death metal">melodic death metal</a> genre, stating that he had wanted to combine <a href="/wiki/Death_metal" title="Death metal">death metal</a> with Iron Maiden's melodic guitar sounds.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetal_Update2010_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetal_Update2010-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other heavy metal artists who cite the band as an influence include <a href="/wiki/Chris_Jericho" title="Chris Jericho">Chris Jericho</a>, a WWE wrestler and lead singer of <a href="/wiki/Fozzy" title="Fozzy">Fozzy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMTV2006(b)_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMTV2006(b)-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cam_Pipes" title="Cam Pipes">Cam Pipes</a>, lead vocalist of <a href="/wiki/3_Inches_of_Blood" title="3 Inches of Blood">3 Inches of Blood</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECharlesworth2009_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECharlesworth2009-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Vitaly Dubinin, bassist of <a href="/wiki/Aria_(band)" title="Aria (band)">Aria</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELenta.ru2010_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELenta.ru2010-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mikael_%C3%85kerfeldt" title="Mikael Åkerfeldt">Mikael Åkerfeldt</a>, guitarist and lead vocalist of <a href="/wiki/Opeth" title="Opeth">Opeth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELawson2013_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELawson2013-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/X_Japan" title="X Japan">X Japan</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Yoshiki_(musician)" title="Yoshiki (musician)">Yoshiki</a> and former guitarist <a href="/wiki/Hide_(musician)" title="Hide (musician)">hide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKakizawa_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKakizawa-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKato_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKato-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Both current and former <a href="/wiki/Dream_Theater" title="Dream Theater">Dream Theater</a> members <a href="/wiki/John_Petrucci" title="John Petrucci">John Petrucci</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Myung" title="John Myung">John Myung</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Portnoy" title="Mike Portnoy">Mike Portnoy</a> have stated that Iron Maiden were one of their biggest influences when their band first formed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010e_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010e-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance_in_media">Appearance in media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Appearance in media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The band's name has been mentioned prominently in several songs, such as the singles "<a href="/wiki/Teenage_Dirtbag" title="Teenage Dirtbag">Teenage Dirtbag</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Wheatus" title="Wheatus">Wheatus</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBasham2000_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBasham2000-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_80%27s_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Back to the 80&#39;s (song)">Back to the 80's</a>" by Danish dance-pop band <a href="/wiki/Aqua_(band)" title="Aqua (band)">Aqua</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetroLyrics(1)_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetroLyrics(1)-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> and "<a href="/wiki/Fat_Lip" title="Fat Lip">Fat Lip</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Sum_41" title="Sum 41">Sum 41</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESputnikmusic(1)_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESputnikmusic(1)-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> Iron Maiden have also been referenced in <a href="/wiki/Weezer" title="Weezer">Weezer</a>'s "Heart Songs" (from their 2008 self-titled "<a href="/wiki/Weezer_(2008_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Weezer (2008 album)">Red</a>" album),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetroLyrics(2)_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetroLyrics(2)-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Blues_Traveler" title="Blues Traveler">Blues Traveler</a>'s "Psycho Joe" (from 1997's <i><a href="/wiki/Straight_On_till_Morning_(album)" title="Straight On till Morning (album)">Straight on till Morning</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetroLyrics(3)_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetroLyrics(3)-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/NOFX" title="NOFX">NOFX</a>'s "Eddie, Bruce and Paul" (from their 2009 album <i><a href="/wiki/Coaster_(album)" title="Coaster (album)">Coaster</a></i>), which <a href="/wiki/Sputnikmusic" title="Sputnikmusic">Sputnikmusic</a> describes as "a humorous retelling of Paul DiAnno's departure".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas2009_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas2009-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, <i><a href="/wiki/Kerrang!" title="Kerrang!">Kerrang!</a></i> released <i><a href="/wiki/Maiden_Heaven:_A_Tribute_to_Iron_Maiden" class="mw-redirect" title="Maiden Heaven: A Tribute to Iron Maiden">Maiden Heaven: A Tribute to Iron Maiden</a></i>, an album composed of Iron Maiden cover songs performed by Metallica, <a href="/wiki/Machine_Head_(band)" title="Machine Head (band)">Machine Head</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dream_Theater" title="Dream Theater">Dream Theater</a>, Trivium, <a href="/wiki/Coheed_and_Cambria" title="Coheed and Cambria">Coheed and Cambria</a>, Avenged Sevenfold, and other groups influenced by the band.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerrang!2008_216-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerrang!2008-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Maiden_uniteD" title="Maiden uniteD">Maiden uniteD</a>, an acoustic tribute band consisting of members of <a href="/wiki/Ayreon" title="Ayreon">Ayreon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Threshold_(band)" title="Threshold (band)">Threshold</a> and <a href="/wiki/Within_Temptation" title="Within Temptation">Within Temptation</a>, released <i><a href="/wiki/Mind_the_Acoustic_Pieces" title="Mind the Acoustic Pieces">Mind the Acoustic Pieces</a></i>, a re-interpretation of the entire <i><a href="/wiki/Piece_of_Mind" title="Piece of Mind">Piece of Mind</a></i> album.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMaiden_United_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMaiden_United-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Many other Iron Maiden cover albums exist (each featuring various artists), including piano,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllMusic_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllMusic-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> electro,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAquarius_Records_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAquarius_Records-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> string quartet<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoftus_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoftus-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> and hip-hop tributes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllMusic(2)_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllMusic(2)-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Iron Maiden songs have been featured in the soundtracks of several video games, including <i><a href="/wiki/Carmageddon_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Carmageddon 2">Carmageddon 2</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGiant_Bomb_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGiant_Bomb-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto:_Vice_City" title="Grand Theft Auto: Vice City">Grand Theft Auto: Vice City</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIGN_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIGN-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto:_Episodes_from_Liberty_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Theft Auto: Episodes from Liberty City">Grand Theft Auto: Episodes from Liberty City</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllgame_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllgame-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto_IV:_The_Lost_and_Damned" title="Grand Theft Auto IV: The Lost and Damned">Grand Theft Auto IV: The Lost and Damned</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERockstar_Games_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERockstar_Games-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Tony_Hawk%27s_Pro_Skater_4" title="Tony Hawk&#39;s Pro Skater 4">Tony Hawk's Pro Skater 4</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2002_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2002-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/SSX_on_Tour" title="SSX on Tour">SSX on Tour</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECheat_Code_Central_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECheat_Code_Central-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Madden_NFL_10" title="Madden NFL 10">Madden NFL 10</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetal_Insider2009_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetal_Insider2009-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Their music also appears in the <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero" title="Guitar Hero">Guitar Hero</a> </i>and <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_Band_(video_game)" title="Rock Band (video game)">Rock Band</a></i> series of <a href="/wiki/Music_video_game" title="Music video game">rhythmic video games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEast2009Rock_Band_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEast2009Rock_Band-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Iron Maiden songs have also appeared in films, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Phenomena_(film)" title="Phenomena (film)">Phenomena</a></i> (entitled <i>Creepers</i> in the US),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBillWyman.com2014_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBillWyman.com2014-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_by_Numbers" title="Murder by Numbers">Murder by Numbers</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoBlo.com_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoBlo.com-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> while MTV's animated duo <a href="/wiki/Beavis_and_Butt-Head" title="Beavis and Butt-Head">Beavis and Butt-Head</a> have commented favourably on the band several times.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWardlawLing2005_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWardlawLing2005-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Transformers_(toy_line)" title="Transformers (toy line)">Transformers</a> author Bill Forster is an avowed Iron Maiden fan and made several Iron Maiden references, including song lyrics and the phrase "Up the Irons" in his books, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Transformers:_The_Ark_:_A_Complete_Compendium_of_Transformers_Animation_Models" class="mw-redirect" title="The Transformers: The Ark : A Complete Compendium of Transformers Animation Models">The Ark</a></i> series and <i>The AllSpark Almanac</i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAngelfire(1)Angelfire(2)_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAngelfire(1)Angelfire(2)-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Claims_of_Satanic_references">Claims of Satanic references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Claims of Satanic references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1982, the band released one of their most popular, controversial and acclaimed albums, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Number_of_the_Beast_(album)" title="The Number of the Beast (album)">The Number of the Beast</a></i>. The artwork and title track led to Christian groups in the United States branding the band as <a href="/wiki/Satanism" title="Satanism">Satanists</a>, encouraging people to destroy copies of the release.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYoung(1)_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYoung(1)-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The band's manager, Rod Smallwood, later commented that Christians initially burnt the records, but later decided to destroy them with hammers through fear of breathing in the melting vinyl's fumes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEagle_Vision2001Young(1)_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEagle_Vision2001Young(1)-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> The protests were not restricted to the US, with Christian organisations preventing Iron Maiden from performing in Chile in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrave_Words_&amp;_Bloody_Knuckles2011(2)_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrave_Words_&amp;_Bloody_Knuckles2011(2)-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Contrary to the accusations, the band have always denied the notion that they are Satanists, with lead vocalist, Bruce Dickinson, doing so on-stage in the <i><a href="/wiki/Live_After_Death" title="Live After Death">Live After Death</a></i> concert video.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEMI2008_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEMI2008-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Steve Harris has since commented that, "It was mad. They completely got the wrong end of the stick. They obviously hadn't read the lyrics. They just wanted to believe all that rubbish about us being Satanists."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004228_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004228-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Harris has also stated that "<a href="/wiki/The_Number_of_the_Beast_(song)" title="The Number of the Beast (song)">The Number of the Beast</a>" song was inspired by a nightmare he had after watching <i><a href="/wiki/Damien:_Omen_II" title="Damien: Omen II">Damien: Omen II</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004224_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004224-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> and also influenced by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Burns" title="Robert Burns">Robert Burns</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Tam_o%27_Shanter_(poem)" title="Tam o&#39; Shanter (poem)">Tam o' Shanter</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEagle_Vision2001_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEagle_Vision2001-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, the band's drummer, <a href="/wiki/Nicko_McBrain" title="Nicko McBrain">Nicko McBrain</a>, has been a born-again Christian since 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGodscare_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGodscare-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ed_Force_One">Ed Force One</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ed Force One">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_757-23A,_Astraeus_AN1497690.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Boeing_757-23A%2C_Astraeus_AN1497690.jpg/220px-Boeing_757-23A%2C_Astraeus_AN1497690.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Boeing_757-23A%2C_Astraeus_AN1497690.jpg/330px-Boeing_757-23A%2C_Astraeus_AN1497690.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Boeing_757-23A%2C_Astraeus_AN1497690.jpg/440px-Boeing_757-23A%2C_Astraeus_AN1497690.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="718" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_757-23A,_Astraeus_AN1497690.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The band's former Ed Force One, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 757-200">Boeing 757-200</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>For their <a href="/wiki/Somewhere_Back_in_Time_World_Tour" title="Somewhere Back in Time World Tour">Somewhere Back in Time World Tour</a> in 2008 and 2009, Iron Maiden commissioned an <a href="/wiki/Astraeus_Airlines" title="Astraeus Airlines">Astraeus Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757</a> as transport.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2008Metal_Storm2007_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2008Metal_Storm2007-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> The aeroplane was converted into a <a href="/wiki/Combi_aircraft" title="Combi aircraft">combi</a> configuration, which enabled it to carry the band, their crew and stage production, thereby allowing the group to perform in countries which were previously deemed unreachable logistically.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetal_Storm2007_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetal_Storm2007-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> It was also repainted with a special Iron Maiden livery,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMetal_Storm2007_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMetal_Storm2007-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> which the airline decided to retain after receiving positive feedback from customers.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2008_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2008-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing747-IronMaiden01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Boeing747-IronMaiden01.jpg/220px-Boeing747-IronMaiden01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Boeing747-IronMaiden01.jpg/330px-Boeing747-IronMaiden01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Boeing747-IronMaiden01.jpg/440px-Boeing747-IronMaiden01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing747-IronMaiden01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iron Maiden's Ed Force One, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a>, as used during The Book of Souls World Tour in 2016.</div></div></div>
<p>The aircraft, named "Ed Force One" after a competition on the band's website,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECashmere2008_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECashmere2008-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> was flown by Dickinson, as he was also a commercial airline pilot for Astraeus, and plays a major role in the award-winning documentary,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJuno_Awards2010Bezer2009c_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJuno_Awards2010Bezer2009c-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden:_Flight_666" title="Iron Maiden: Flight 666">Iron Maiden: Flight 666</a></i>, which was released in cinemas in 42 countries in April 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBezer2009a_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBezer2009a-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> A different aeroplane (registered G-STRX)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEMI2012_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEMI2012-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> was used for <a href="/wiki/The_Final_Frontier_World_Tour" title="The Final Frontier World Tour">The Final Frontier World Tour</a> in 2011 with altered livery, adopting the artwork of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Final_Frontier" title="The Final Frontier">The Final Frontier</a></i> album,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010d_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2010d-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> and features heavily in the 2012 documentary "<a href="/wiki/En_Vivo!_(Iron_Maiden_album)" title="En Vivo! (Iron Maiden album)">Behind the Beast</a>". For <a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Souls_World_Tour" title="The Book of Souls World Tour">The Book of Souls World Tour</a> in 2016, the band upgraded to an ex-<a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> jumbo jet, supplied by <a href="/wiki/Air_Atlanta_Icelandic" title="Air Atlanta Icelandic">Air Atlanta Icelandic</a> (registered TF-AAK)<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPlaneSpotters.netSands2016_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPlaneSpotters.netSands2016-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> and customised by <a href="/wiki/Volga-Dnepr_Airlines" title="Volga-Dnepr Airlines">Volga-Dnepr Gulf</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEvolga-dnepr.com2016_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEvolga-dnepr.com2016-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> which allows for more space without the aircraft having to undergo a significant conversion to carry their equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELach2015b_192-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELach2015b-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style_and_influences">Musical style and influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Musical style and influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:IronMaidenRTTH.ogg" title="File:IronMaidenRTTH.ogg">"Run to the Hills" (1982)</a></div>

<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>Steve Harris, Iron Maiden's bassist and primary songwriter,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMusicRadar2010_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMusicRadar2010-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> has stated that his influences include <a href="/wiki/Black_Sabbath" title="Black Sabbath">Black Sabbath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">Deep Purple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uriah_Heep_(band)" title="Uriah Heep (band)">Uriah Heep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)" title="Genesis (band)">Genesis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yes_(band)" title="Yes (band)">Yes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jethro_Tull_(band)" title="Jethro Tull (band)">Jethro Tull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thin_Lizzy" title="Thin Lizzy">Thin Lizzy</a>, <a href="/wiki/UFO_(band)" title="UFO (band)">UFO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wishbone_Ash" title="Wishbone Ash">Wishbone Ash</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2004cEMI2004Wall200427Wall2004154_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2004cEMI2004Wall200427Wall2004154-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 Harris stated, "I think if anyone wants to understand Maiden's early thing, in particular the harmony guitars, all they have to do is listen to Wishbone Ash's <i><a href="/wiki/Argus_(album)" title="Argus (album)">Argus</a></i> album. Thin Lizzy too, but not as much. And then we wanted to have a bit of a prog thing thrown in as well, because I was really into bands like Genesis and Jethro Tull. So you combine all that with the heavy riffs and the speed, and you've got it."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBienstock2011_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBienstock2011-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Harris explained that the band's "heaviness" was inspired by "Black Sabbath and Deep Purple with a bit of Zeppelin thrown in."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2004c_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlabbermouth.net2004c-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> On top of this, Harris developed his own playing style, which guitarist Janick Gers describes as "more like a rhythm guitar,"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPopoff2005(c)_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPopoff2005(c)-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> cited as responsible for the band's galloping style,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFender_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFender-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> heard in such songs as "<a href="/wiki/The_Trooper" title="The Trooper">The Trooper</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuey(2)_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuey(2)-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> and "Run to the Hills."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELawson_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELawson-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The band's guitarists, Dave Murray, Adrian Smith, and Janick Gers, each have their own individual influences and playing style. Dave Murray is known for his <a href="/wiki/Legato" title="Legato">legato</a> technique which, he claims, "evolved naturally. I'd heard <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a> using legato when I was growing up, and I liked that style of playing."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcIver2010(a)_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcIver2010(a)-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Stating that he "was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Blues_rock" title="Blues rock">blues rock</a> rather than metal," Adrian Smith was influenced by <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Winter" title="Johnny Winter">Johnny Winter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pat_Travers" title="Pat Travers">Pat Travers</a>, leading to him becoming a "melodic player."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcIver2010(c)_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcIver2010(c)-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> Janick Gers, on the other hand, prefers a more improvised style, largely inspired by <a href="/wiki/Ritchie_Blackmore" title="Ritchie Blackmore">Ritchie Blackmore</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004277_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004277-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> which he claims is in contrast to Smith's "rhythmic" sound.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcIver2010(b)_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcIver2010(b)-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Singer Bruce Dickinson, who typically works in collaboration with guitarist Adrian Smith,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004244_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004244-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> has an operatic vocal style, inspired by <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Brown_(musician)" title="Arthur Brown (musician)">Arthur Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Hammill" title="Peter Hammill">Peter Hammill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Anderson" title="Ian Anderson">Ian Anderson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ian_Gillan" title="Ian Gillan">Ian Gillan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDmme.net_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDmme.net-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> and is often considered to be one of the best heavy metal vocalists of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERosen2011HearYa.com2006Blabbermouth.net2009aBlabbermouth.net2009b_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERosen2011HearYa.com2006Blabbermouth.net2009aBlabbermouth.net2009b-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> Although Nicko McBrain has only received one writing credit, on the <i>Dance of Death</i> album,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELing2005b_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELing2005b-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> Harris often relies on him while developing songs. Adrian Smith commented, "Steve loves playing with him. [They] used to work for hours going over these bass and drum patterns."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004241_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004241-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout their career, the band's style has remained largely unchanged, in spite of the addition of guitar synthesisers on 1986's <i>Somewhere in Time</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPrato_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPrato-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> keyboards on 1988's <i>Seventh Son of a Seventh Son</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004265_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004265-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and an attempt to return to the "stripped down" production of their earlier material on 1990's <i>No Prayer for the Dying</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004283_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004283-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In recent years, however, the band have begun using more <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive</a> elements in their songs,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDome2006aDome2006b_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDome2006aDome2006b-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> which Steve Harris describes as not progressive "in the modern sense, but like <a href="/wiki/Dream_Theater" title="Dream Theater">Dream Theater</a>, more in a 70s way".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDome2006b_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDome2006b-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> According to Harris, <i>Seventh Son of a Seventh Son</i> was the band's first album which was "more progressive",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004264_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004264-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> while they would only return to this style from 1995's <i>The X Factor</i>, which he states is "like an extension of <i>Seventh Son</i>..., in the sense of the progressive element to it".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWall2004311_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWall2004311-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The development contrasts with the band's raw-sounding earlier material,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBienstock2011_215-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBienstock2011-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> which <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> states was "clearly drawing from elements of punk rock",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuey(1)_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuey(1)-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> although Harris firmly denies this.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVH12011_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVH12011-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Band_members">Band members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Maiden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Band members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li><a href="/wiki/Dave_Murray_(musician)" title="Dave Murray (musician)">Dave Murray</a> – <a href="/wiki/Electric_guitar" title="Electric guitar">guitars</a> <small>(1976–1977, 1978–present)</small></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Bruce_Dickinson" title="Bruce Dickinson">Bruce Dickinson</a> – <a href="/wiki/Lead_vocalist" title="Lead vocalist">lead vocals</a> <small>(1981–1993, 1999–present)</small>, <a href="/wiki/Piano" title="Piano">piano</a> <small>(2015)</small></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nicko_McBrain" title="Nicko McBrain">Nicko McBrain</a> – <a href="/wiki/Drum_kit" title="Drum kit">drums</a> <small>(1982–present)</small></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Janick_Gers" title="Janick Gers">Janick Gers</a> – guitars <small>(1990–present)</small></li></ul>
<p><b>Touring musicians</b>
</p>
<ul><li>Michael Kenney – keyboards <small>(1988–present)</small></li></ul>
<p>&#32;
